Subject: Criminal Procedure

Delivery Date: 1970-01-01

 

 

Code of Criminal Procedure, 1898

[Act No. V of 1898]

 

Section-167(5)

The amended provision of section 167(5)- the provisions of section (5) of section 167 Cr. P. C. is undoubtedly a procedural law. The Criminal Procedure Code (Second Amendment) Act, 1992 (Act XLII of 1992) did not make any provision that the amendment brought in section 167, although a procedural law, will operate prospectively- operates retrospectively.

Kali Pada Dutta Vs. Subal Chandra Dev & Anr 6 BLT (AD)-244

Section-167 (5)

Accused cannot claim the privilege of bail as a matter of right—Section 167 (5) of the Code of Criminal Procedure enjoins that if investigation is not concluded within 120 days from the date of receipt of the information relating to the commission of the offence, the court, if satisfied can release the accused on bail. BLT the accused cannot claim the privilege of bail as a matter of right. In the face of peculiar circumstances, delay in completion of investigation of the case is no ground to release the accused-petitioner on bail.

Major (Retd) M. Khairuzzaman Vs. The State 6 BLT (HCD)-130

Section-167(5)

In the instant case further extension of time for further investigation was not obtained from the Sessions Judge after 6.7.1992-under the repealed sub- section (6) of section 167 Cr. P. C. was the Sessions Judge who had directed further investigation into the offences after the expiry of the period mentioned in sub- section (5)- BLT with the amendment of Section 167 Cr. P.C. by Act 42 of 1992, the time limit for conclusion of investigation was done away with and the amendment being in respect of a Procedural Law.

Govt. of Bangladesh Vs. Shah Alam 3 BLT  (AD)-172

Section-167(5)

Support of bail—regard being had to the part played by accused petitioner in commission of crime and nature of injury manifested in post mortem report and long delay in completion of investigation, we are of this considered view that the accused petitioner made out a case for his being released on bail.

Md. Mosiur Rahman Vs. The State 9BLT (HCD)-387

Section-169

Section 169 of the Code of Criminal Procedure has not given the police officer any power to judge the credibility of the witnesses and to decide the defence plea of alibi.

Abdur Rouf & Ors Vs. Jalaluddin & Anr 6BLT(AD)-172

Section-172

Case diary—it appears that the High Court Division directed the Investigating Officer to put in an affidavit with copies of the pages of the diary which is against the provision of law and as such illegal. It cannot be said by any stretch of imagination that for transparency of investigation a case diary or any part thereof may be put in before any court of law by way of affidavit. Such contention is not supported by any law and the High Court Division by directing the Investigation Officer to swear affidadit along with copies of certain pages of the diary has acted illegally which cannot be supported.

Bangladesh & Ors. Vs. Dr. Shamima Sultana Rita 10 BLT (AD)-160

Section-173

When second charge sheet appears to be a result not of a further investigation, it is re­investigation. There cannot be any re­investigation into a case after chargesheet have been submitted.

Afia Khatoon Vs. Mobasswir Ali & Ors. 3 BLT (AD)-74

Section-173

Supplementary charge sheet- Police can always file supplementary charge sheet even after acceptance of the previous charge sheet. There is no limitation in this regard or taboo in the law.

Sultan Ahmed Vs. The State 3 BLT (HCD)-162

Section-173

It is on record that the case was twice investigated once by the local police and then by the Criminal Investigation Department and the investigation officers took into consideration the post-mortem report wherein Medical Officer opined that the death of the deceased was accidental and also the fact that the petitioner did not adduce any evidence before the investigating officer or the Criminal Investigation Department and also the other facts and circumstances of the case. The High Court Division it appears found that the Naraji petition of the petitioner was not supported by any materials. The High Court Division accordingly on consideration of the facts and circumstances of the case and relevant materials on record rejected the naraji petition—No illegality in Passing the impugned order.

Md. Farid Miah Chowdhury Vs. Mrs. Jahanara Begum & Ors 12 BLT (AD)-221

Section -173

An witness once narrated the occurrence without implicating the appellant with the offence in any manner cannot be permitted to depose for the second time with a view to implicating the accused and play double standard. Such allowance in our view will encourage implication of a innocent person into false charge in the hands unscrupulous interested elements and it will frustrate the purpose of further investigation.

Ruhul Amin Kha Vs. The State 13 BLT (HCD)-66

Section-173(l) and 171

The responsibilities of the investigating agencies in general

The functions of the police officer to ensure the attendance of the witnesses at the trial of a case is a statutory responsibility. The police officer cannot avoid this responsibility. His responsibility is not over as soon as he completed the investigation and submitted the police report i.e. charge sheet. BLT his responsibility continues till the conclusion of the trial to see that no evidence in the case is lost by means of gaining over a witness or otherwise, which may happen in case of delay in holding trial of a case.

Daily Star & Protham Alo Patrika Vs. The State 9 BLT (HCD)-91

Section-173(3A) read with The Police Regulation

In the present case the statements recorded under Section 161 Cr. P.C. have not been sent to the trial along with the record. The learned Deputy Attorney General submits that those were kept with the prosecution for safety reasons BLT that submission cannot be accepted. If the prosecution fells that those may be interpolated they may pray for keeping those in the safe custody of the trial court. These statement are vital documents and these cannot be withheld from the defence. These may be necessary for the defence to make out their own case. The accused has every right to look into these statements before any hearing takes place. For the ends of justice and for transparency in the trial these documents cannot be withheld and what has been done in the present case cannot be supported by any stretch of imagination. The prosecution in such a case is bound to send the statements recorded under Section 161 of the Code of Criminal Procedure along with the police report to the trial court. They cannot withhold these. We fail to understand why in this case the prosecution is playing hide and seek. The attitude of the prosecuting agencies is far from satisfactory. If the prosecution wants transparency in the trial they must come with clean hands. Any withholding of such documents will definitely affect the result of the case and this will cause prejudice to the defence. It appears that hearing under section 265 of the Code of Criminal Procedure in respect of the petitioners of Criminal Petition No. 69 of 2000 is yet to be completed and in such circumstances before that date the originals should be produced before the trial court and if the prosecution fails to produce those the court may take adverse view on the genuineness or otherwise of the statements.

Major (Retd.) Bazlul Huda & Ors. Vs. The State 9 BLT (AD)-58

Section-173 Sub-section 3(B)

The High Court in its judgment dated 17.6.2003 rightly held that the Naraji petition being a fresh complaint the Additional Metropolitan Sessions Judge did not commit any illegality in directing the Magistrate to send the case to the police for further investigation as it has disclosed some evidence against the accused persons.

Md. Saidur Rahman Shahid Vs The State 14 BLT (AD)-119

Section -173 (3B)

We are of the view that filing of naraji petition does not debar a Magistrate from directing further investigation after a police report under Section 173 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is submitted by the investigating agency.

Kamal Uddin Vs. The State 15 BLT (AD)-107

Section- 173(3B) read with Narcotics Control Act, 1990, Section-39

Whether a letter written by the Director General of Narcotics Control requested to the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate for further investigation, treated as Naraji Petition.

High Court Division setting aside the Order of further investigation passed by the Court below -Held; the High Court Division having not taken into consideration of the facts and law legally decided the case without proper appreciation of the principle of law involved in the instant case. The learned Judges of the High Court Division committed serious error of law in setting aside the judgment and order of the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka for further investigation.

The State Vs. A. K. M. Saiful Islam 15 BLT (AD)299

Sections -173, 190

We are of the opinion that there is nothing either in section 173 or in section 190 of the Code of Criminal Procedure Providing for rejection or acceptance of a police report there is also nothing to show that sue' police report is binding upon a Magistrate.

Delwar Hossain Vs. The State 4 BLT (HCD)-144

Section-174

Disposal of the dead body

Statement in the Inquest Report as to ascertainment of the cause of death is thus admissible in evidence and that can becharacterized as the best evidence.

Sharafat Mondal & Ors. Vs. The State & Ors 14 BLT (HCD)-290

Section-174

Inquest is mandatory if a Person died under suspicious circumstances.

The ocular accounts supplied by PW 3, PW 6 and PW 7 in fixing the place in front of  the house of Gaffar Shaheb at 20/S,K.M. Azam Lane as the scene of occurrence stand pulverized by the Inquest Report wherein place in front of "Mia Bari" had been marked as the place of occurrence. All these throw a patent doubt whether the incident had actually taken place in the manner 'and the  place as suggested by prosecution and the statement embodied in Inquest Report knocked the bottom out of the prosecution case and embroilment of convict-appellants in the felony.

Rustum & Ors Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD)-435

Section- 179(C)

Criminal Acts of accused Nos. 3 & 4 by way of obtaining signatures of the complainant in papers at Jeddah money was withdrawn in Bangladesh- Criminal Court in Bangladesh can take cognizance of the offences.

Abdus  Sattar Vs. The State & Anr 6BLT (AD)-144

Section-181(2)

A case under Section 406 of the Penal Code may also be tried by a Court within the jurisdiction of which the property or part of it was received or retained.

Anwar Hossain & Anr. Vs. The State & Ors. 10 BLT (HCD)-102

Section-190

Cognizance- Sessions Judge cannot take cognizance of the case against the accused sentup in the supplementary charge sheet directly without cognizance being taken by the Magistrate under Section 190 of the Code of Criminal procedure.

Sultan Ahmed Vs. The State 3 BLT (HCD)-162

Section-190(1)(b)

Cognizance—the learned Judge of the Bishesh Adalat ought to have applied his mind in the allegations made in the charge sheet and also in the materials on record as envisaged under Section 173(l)(a). Section 173(3A) and Section 190(l)(b) of the Code including if necessary, the case diary itself, so as to satisfy himself about the prima facie evidence against the accused persons and also about the probabilities of their guilt—the Magistrate must examine those materials and apply his mind before taking decision under Section 190(l)(b) of the Code however painstaking such exercise may appear to be, otherwise, the purpose for insertion of Sub-Section 3A would be frustrated and will be a fruitless idle formality.

The State Vs. Md. Joynal Abdein & Ors 8 BLT (HCD)-376

Section -190 & 193

Under sections 190, 193 Cr.P.C. no court of sessions shall take cognizance of any offence as a court of original jurisdiction unless accused has been sent to it by the Magistrate duly empowered in behalf.

Md. Nurul Amin Vs. Zahirul Islam & Ors 14 BLT (HCD)-462

Section-193

Section 193 of the Code bars Court of Sessions from taking cognizance of any offence as a Court of original jurisdiction unless the accused had been sent to it by a Magistrate duly empowered in that behalf.

Eman Ullah Vs. Abdul Kader & Anr. 11 BLT (HCD)-6

Section-195 and 476

The Sub-Divisional Officer made the complaint on a perusal of the petition filed by the petitioner to him and also on a perusal of the case record of Misc Case No. 2357-N/72-73. Before making such complaint, the Sub Divisional Officer did not hold any preliminary inquiry required by law for ascertaining the truth or falsehood of the allegations made by the petitioner. The learned Magistrate also look cognizance of the offence without ascertaining as to whether the complaint discloses any offence referred to Section 195 (1) clause (b) or clause (c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure. We are, therefore of the opinion that the learned Magistrate drew up the proceeding mechanically without application of his judicial mind.

Abul Hashem Hawlader Vs. The State 8 BLT (HCD)-292

Section-195

In the present case admittedly the Hebabil-Ewaz dated 25.03.1974 was given in evidence in O.C. Suit No. 18 of 1977 in the Court of Munsif—Held : No court can take cognizance of any offence under Section 467of the Penal Code without complaint in writing by the concerned court in which such court is subordinate in terms of Section 195 of the Code of Criminal Procedue.

Akkas Ali Vs. The State 10 BLT (HCD)-478

Section - 195(1)(a)

In the instant case it appears that the process server himself submitted his report and the report has been forwarded to the learned Magistrate. - We are of the view that in order to satisfy himself as to the report of the process server, the learned Senior Assistant Judge examined the materials and being satisfied thereof, sent the report to the learned Magistrate for necessary action and thus there is no illegality in the aforesaid steps of the learned Assistant Judge taken for prima - facie satisfaction of him.

AKM Samsuddin doctor & Anr Vs. The State 14 BLT (AD)-22

Section- 195(1)(C)

Section 195(l)(c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure has reference only to a forged document and not to a copy of it. The Court before which a copy of a forged document is produced is not in a position to determine the genuineness or otherwise of the questioned deed in the absence of the original. The production of the certified copy of a forged document does not, therefore invoke the bar of section 195(1)(c) of the Code.

Md. Nuruddin Ahmed & Ors. Vs. The State 6 BLT (HCD)-217

Section -195 (1) (C)

Whether the private complaint in respect offence under sections 467/471 of the Pen Code during the pendency of a civil suit j barred under section 195 (I) (c) of the Co of Criminal Procedure.

Section 195 (I) (c) of the Code Criminal Procedure provides that in ca where the alleged forged deeds have be produced or given in evidence in any Court the Institution of the Criminal Case is barred the basis of a private complaint.

Md. Takumuddin Par Vs. The State 4BLT (AD)-84

 

Section- 195(1)(C)

Accusation of committing offences under sections 409/420/467 of the Penal Code and under Section 5(2) of Act 11 of 1947- the title suit against the Government and others in respect of the disputed land is pending Held: As cognizance was taken not only under Section 467 of the Penal Code BLT also under Sections 409 and 420 of the Penal Code and under Section 5(2) of Act 11 of 1947 and as such the Criminal case is not barred under section 195(l)(c) Cr.P.C.

Md. Sadat Ali Talukder Vs. The State & Anr 7 BLT (AD)-342

Section-195 (1) (C)

The offence committed by the accused is the misappropriation of the amount of T.A. bills of the witnesses withdrawn from the bank after preparing fictitious T.A. bills which are purely an administrative matter not part of any judicial proceedings. So, the above provisions are not applicable.

Md. Abu Sufian Mia Vs. The State 7 BLT (HCD)-26

Section-195(1)(c)

Since before initiation of the Criminal case i.e CR. Case No. 174 of 1993 the deed had been produced and used before the Civil Court in support prayed for in the suit and t the suit in which said deed has been used still pending and consequently the genuineness or otherwise of the relating to which criminal proceeding had been at the instance of the Respondent No. 2, who is a ' in the suit as defendant, awaits adjudication, as such because of the vision of clause (c) of Sub-section (1) of Section 195 of the Code of Criminal Procedure the respondent No. 2 at his level is from initiating criminal proceeding on allegation that the deed dated January 8, 6 is a forged one. Even if on the 'nation of trial of the Title Suit the document in question is found by the court otherwise than being genuine then also Respondent no. 2 under the law would not be competent to initiate criminal on the allegation deed in question is forged as had been given in evidence in trial.

Md. Abu Daud Sarder Vs. The Sate & Anr. UBLT(AD)-47

Section-195(l)(c)

Forged deed was filed for the purpose of mutation it would not be barred under Section 195(l)(c) of the Code of Criminal Procedure because the Upazilla Revenue Officer did not perform the function of revenue
court when dealing with a mutation case.

Md. Rabi Shaikh @ Rabi Shaikh & Anr. Vs. The State 11BLT (AD)-1

Section-195 (1)(c) read with Section-476

Having full knowledge that the deed was forged, fraudulent and created, DW_1 Abdul Awal Minto on behalf of defendant no. 14 gave the deed into evidence, DW_1 Abdul Awal Minto thereby committed a serious offence making him liable for prosecution under Section 195(1)(c) read with section 476 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

M/S. N.F.M. Universeum Estate Ltd. Vs Gulshan Begum & Ors. 14 BLT (HCD)-225

Section-195(1)(c)

The Criminal Court could not take cognizance of the case unless the said Court itself is the complainant and in the absence of such complaint the entire proceeding is vitiated.

Rafique Fakir & Ors Vs. Alhaj Mollah Faroz Ahmed 15 BLT (AD)239

Section-195 (1) (c)

Subsequent report -In the instant case, though cognizance was taken upon examination of the complainant and a subsequent report of the Assistant Revenue Office BLT the said report is not a substitute to a complaint contemplated under section 195(1)(C) of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

Rafique Fakir & Ors Vs. Alhaj Mollah Faroz Ahmed 15 BLT (AD) 239

Section-199

Offence U/S 497/498 — Section 199 Cr. P. C. provides for leave of the Court to lodge complaint when any person other than the husband, having care of the wife on behalf of the husband at the time when offences under Section 497 and 498 P.C. was committed. Any such complaint without such leave is to maintainable. There must be an application for leave to lodge the complaint and material to show that it granted. Leave to lodge the complaint cannot be presumed or implied. Reference in his regard may be made to the decision in AIR 1933 Cal. 880.

Md. Mohsin Ali Khan Vs. Shams-F-Ara Binte Huda & Ors.   11 BLT (AD)-10

Section -200

Cognizance without examining the complainant - In the present case cognizance was taken on the basis of the judicial inquiry and as such examination of the complainant was not necessary - Petition is dismissed.

Md. Alim Vs. Noor Mohammad Bepari & Anr. 4 BLT (AD)-257

Section- 200

After receiving the petition of complaint the learned Magistrate proceeded under section 202 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and himself held the judicial inquiry and in that inquiry the complainant was examined, the action of the learned Magistrate has not vitiated the proceedings in any way to not examining  the  complainant immediately after filing of Naraji Petition.

Delwar Hossain Vs. The State 4 BLT (HCD)-144

Section-200

Naraji petition — Held: In this case we] have noticed that the learned Magistrate has rejected the Naraji petitions without examining the complainant petitioner. It is now settled that a naraji petition is a complaint in all practial purposes and therefore, as soon as the naraji petition is filed, the learned Magistrate is required to examine the complainant on S.A. and if he finds a prima-facie case against the accused persons he may take cognizance against them and if he did not find a prima-facie case, he may send the complaint for inquiry as observed earlier, for ascertaining the truth; or falsedhood of the complaint.

Maksuda Begum Vs. Abu Taleb Molla & Ors 9 BLT (HCD)-449

 

Section-200

When the final report was submitted the informant filed a Narazi petition and according^ to law there ought to have been a judicial inquiry BLT instead of doing that cognizance wad taken which is illegal as contended by the petitioners Counsel.

Held : It is well settled that when the police! submits a report in the form of final repot a Magistrate is not bound to accept that report.] He may act on the basis of that police report] in taking congnizance and that has been] done in the present case. The High Court Division considered this aspect of the matter and came to the finding that there is no illegality in the order of the learned Magistrate in taking cognizance. It appears! that no Narazi petition was filed with the Magistrate before acceptance of the police report. In such a situation the procedure id is legal.

Abdul Aziz Sarder Vs. The State 10 BLT (AD)-34

 

Section -200 read with Section 561A

The informant filed the Naraji Petition against the report so far it is relates to the present petitioner, whereupon the learned Judge of the Tribunal without examining the complainant as required in section 200 Cr.P.C. accepted the Naraji Petition and issued process against the accused petitoners, which is illegal inasmuch as it is settled that the Naraji Petition is to be treated as a fresh complaint and therefore,taking cognizance in accepting Naraji Petition without examining the complainant under on 200 Cr.P.C. is obviously illegal.

Jannatul Ferdous@ Kushum & Anr Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD) 567

 

Section-200 read with 202

The object of section 200 of the code of Criminal procedure is to protect public against false, frivolous and vexatious complaints filed against them in Criminal courts and the Magistrate must not lightly accept written complaint and proceed to issue processes until he is fully convinced about the genuineness of the allegation made against the accused and is to be satisfied that a prima facie case had been made out against those who were accused of criminal offences. Examination of the complaint  under  section  200  Code of Criminal Procedure is not mere form BLT an intelligent enquiry into the subject matter of complaint carried far enough to enable magistrate to exercise his judgment as to where there is or there is no sufficient ground for proceeding -The object of the provision of 202 is to enable the Magistrate to form an opinion as to whether process would be issued or not. The scope of enquiry is only to find out whether is a prima facie case. The Magistrate should keep in mind that justice should not only be done BLT it should appear to have done.

Alhaj  Abdul Kashem Vs. The State 15 BLT (HCD)-227

 

Section-202

Judicial inquiry is an independent inquiry and as such an inquiry is held under provisions of section 202 of the Code and it does not amount to re-opening of a case.

Delwar Hossain Vs. The State 4 BLT (HCD)-144

 

Section-202

The presence of high Police officer and Police representative during Judicial Inquiry to be performed by a Magistrate under Section 202 of the Code of Criminal Procedure when the Police personnels stand arraigned as accused for commission of crime is absolutely impermissible in the interest of fair inquiry and hearing and also contrary to law, procedure and justice.

Moni Begum @ Moni Vs. M. Shamsur Rahman & Ors 10 BLT (HCD)-70

 

Section-202(2A)

Whether on the same occurrence two cases arose—tried simultaneously.

It is well settled that when over the same occurrence cases, one police case and another complaint two case, against different sets of accused person with different versions arose, would be tried simultaneously by the same court. In view of that seceled  practice of trial of cross cases if in the instant case after holding enquiry complaying the provisions of section 202(2A) of the code of Criminal Procedure the learned Magistrate takes cognizance of the offence on the petition of complaint against the accused persons he will send the case to the court of session and then the complaint case will be tried simultaneously with the sessions case initiated on police report by the same court. For that end further proceeding of the Sessions case should remain stayed till sending the case to the court of Sessions in case of taking cognizance of the offence on the petition of complaint.

A. Rob Munshi Vs. The State 13 BLT (HCD)493

 

Section 203

It is seen from the material on record the Magistrate who held the enquiry weighed the evidence and thereupon made recommendation for dismissal of the petition of complaint. On receipt of the report from the Magistrate who held enquiry, the chief Metropolitan Magistrate without examining the evidence on record at his level merely relying on the recommendation of the Additional Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, who held enquiry in the complaint and recommended for dismissal, dismissed the petition of complaint. The order of the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate being not based on independent consideration of the evidence collected during the enquiry, the High Court Division was quite correct in setting aside the order passed by the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate dismissing the petition of complaint filed by the respondents No. 1 and thereupon in making direction for holding fresh enquiry into the complaint of the respondents No. 1.

Md. Akbar Hossain Vs. Hasanul Hoque Enu & Ors 11 BLT (AD)-166

 

Section - 205 (1)

After the dismissed of the petition of complaint under section 203Cr. P.C. the informant-respondent's remedy was to approach the higher court under section 436 Cr. P.C. for further enquiry into his petition of complaint. Neither the Sessions Judge nor the High Court Division is invested with any power to direct any Magistrate to take cognizance of a case. Their power is strictly limited to directing a further enquiry into the petition of complaint. It will be for the Magistrate concerned to take or not to take cognizance after the result of further enquiry - The penultimate order of the High Court Division in directing the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate to take cognizance with section 205(1) Cr. P. C. is therefore not, sustainable in Law.

Yusuf A. Hassan Vs. K.M. Razaul Firdous. 4 BLT (AD)-85

 

Section-205 D

When in a case instituted on a complaint, it is made to appear before the Magistrate during the course of the enquiry or trial that an investigation by the police is the subject of the inqurity, held by him, the Magistrate shall stay the proceeding of the inquiry and call for a report on the matter from the officer in charge conducting the investigation. If the report is* submittd under Section 173, basing upon which, cognizance of offence is taken by any Magistrate against any person who is an accused in the complaint case, the Magistrate shall inquir or try both the cases as if both the cases were instituted on a police report, In however, police report does not relate to any accused to a complaint case or if the Magistrate does not take cognizance of an offence on the police report, he shall proceed with the inquiry or trial which was stayed by him in accordance with the provision of the Code.

Maksuda Begum Vs. Abu Taleb Molla & Ors 9 BLT (HCD)-449

 

Section - 222 read with Penal Code, 1860 Section - 302

No charge was framed for abetting the offence of murder. Even at the time of examining him under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure his attention was not drawn to the evidence of P.Ws. 1-3 that at his order other accused persons committed the offence of murder. So conviction of Abul Kalam under section 302 of the Penal Code is founded on no legal evidence. There is also no convincing evidence that he abetted the murder and thereby committed an offence punishable under section 302/114 of the Penal Code.

Abul Kalam & Ors. Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD)214

Muhibur Rahman Manik & Anr Vs. The Sate 15 BLT (HCD)279

 

Sections- 227 & 231 read With Cruelty to Women (Deterrent Punishment) Ordinance, 1983 Sections 4 and 8A read with 25D of the Special Powers Act.

Any Court may alter or add to any charge at any time before judgment is pronounced subject  to  the  mandatory  provision of section 231 of the code as soon as the altered charge was read over, the accused pleaded  not guilty  and prayed for an opportunity to further cross-examine all the P.Ws. by filing an application to that effect which the tribunal readily allowed. Held: When the Special Tribunal allowed the appellants prayer for further cross-examination of all P.Ws. as provided for in Section 231 there was no scope of his being prejudiced.

Abu Bakker Vs The State 3 BLT (HCD)-98

Section-233, 234,235 and 239

Joinder of charges and Misjoiner of charges

Sections-233, 234, 235 and 239 of the Code are exception to the general rule that for every distinct offence there shall be a separate charge and every such charge shall be tried separately. The object of the exceptions is to avoid the necessarily of the same witnesses giving the same evidence over and over again at different trials. Misjoinder of charges is an illegality which is not curable under Section-537 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

Abdul Jalil Vs. The State 9 BLT (HCD)-5

Section-233 read with Section-239

"Same transaction" and the persons involved in the incidents are "accused of the same offences"

In the instant case it is the prosecution case that petitioner and others encircled the house of the victims and thereupon from amongst the persons who encircled the house of the victims the petitioner and some others entered into the hut wherein the victims — the element of continuity of action was also present in the instant case in that the petitioner and others encircled the house of the victims and that thereafter petitioner and some others entered into the hut of the victims and caused injuries by sharp cutting weapons in consequence whereof the death occurred. In this state of the matter it can in no way be said that the offences or in other wards causing death of the two persons by the petitioner and others was not committed or done in the course of the "same transaction" or in one transaction.

Delower Hossain Khan Vs. The State 11 BLT (AD)-12

Section - 238

The alteration of the conviction from a schedule offence to an offence which is only referable under Penal Code is not legally permissible. Alteration of the conviction under Section 342/34 of the Penal Code cannot be legally and lawfully done while disposing of an appeal arising from the; jurisdiction of the Special Tribunal under Section 30 of the Act.

Abdur Rahman & Ors. Vs. The State 7 BLT (AD)-225

Section-239

Prosecution case is that acting on a tip-off, P.W. 5,6,7,8,9,10,11,12,and 14 along with other police personnel laid siege the house on Siddique Mia of 82 Hazaribagh, apprehended appellants khokan and Swapan, recovered some Arm, ammunition and bombs from their possession, while other appellants fled away by firing and hurling bombs aiming the police force, causing injuries to P.Ws 5,8,11,14 including Khokan. According to the prosecution, the accused persons were taking preparation to commit dacoity to the businessmen of Hazaribag. One case has been instituted under sections 399/402 of the Penal Code: and the other under sections 332/333/353/34 of the Penal Code. The offences were! committed in course of the same transaction -The learned Assistant Judge overlooked^ this provision of law and unnecessarily* wasted Court's valuable time in holding trial of two cases. Similarly, the investigating officer (P.W. 14) and the public prosecutor failed to point out this defect and wasted their energy twice, which could have been avoided.

Bura Yunus & Ors Vs. the State 15 BLT (HCD)-383

Section-241A

The Audit report at the stage of framing of the change- Accused- petitioner was discharged under Section 241A of the Code of Criminal Procedure by the learned Additional District Magistrate- Held: While framing the charge extraneous materials could not be considered at all- the petition is dismissed.

Section-241A

Allegations under section 282 of companies Act-in such criminal matters before framing of the charge the Magistrate is bound to hear the parties under section 241A of the Code of Criminal Procedure and on consideration of the record of the case and the documents submitted if the Magistrate  considers  the  charge  to be groundless he shall discharge the accused.

Mr. Shamsul Haque Vs. Mr. Tamizul Haque & Ors.   13 BLT (AD)229

In the instant case the FIR the charge sheet the Medical report were on record. Interpretation of Statue

Discharge of the accuseds where the police fails to complete investigation and submit the report or the Magistrate failing to complete the trial within certain time or dealing with a petition of complaint by the Magistrate in a case triable by the Court of Sessions, the omission enquiry under chapter XVIII and the other provisions such as trial accused in absentia, the introduction of 439 A and 439 (4), appeal against the inadequacy sentence by the State and the complainant and the amendment of Section 439(4). In a complaint case had altered the basic structure and character of the Code.

Abdul J alii & Ors. Vs. The State 2 BLT(HCD)-90

(b) The Principle of Criminal Jurisprudence or the Principle of Natural Justice requires that the accused be identified on the dock by the witnesses least there is a measure of justice. BLT neither the High Court Division nor the Appellate Division relating to trial in the absence of the accused. This is now a normal affair.

Abdul Jalil & Ors. Vs. The State 2BLT (HCD)-90

Section-241A, 265C

The Learned Divisional Special Judge should discharge the accused persons solely on the basis of the complaint petition and the other materials on record

The learned Judge discharged the accused persons considering the some other grounds which were not available either in the complaint petition or in the record. So, it is held that the learned Special Judge acted beyond his jurisdiction be that it under section 241A or 265C of the Code of Criminal Procedure by illegally relying upon some extraneous materials which were not in the record. So, the order of discharge is illegal.

Abid Hossain Babu Vs. Gazi Mojibul Hoque & Ors. 7 BLT (HCD)-33

Section- 241A, 265C & 561A

  The High Court Division can quash the proceeding of a Criminal case under section 561A Cr.P.C. even during police investigation if no cognizable offence is disclosed - this view has been approved in the case of Emperor invoked 561A Cr. P. C. before availing of the remedy provided in 241A Cr. P. C. and 265 C Cr. P. C has been disapproved by the Supreme Court Appellate Division as being not correct.

Hashim Vs. The State 3 BLT (AD) -129

Section- 243

The provisions of section 243 Cr.P.C. are mandatory and in violation of the same, the so-called admission or pleading of guilt of the accused appellant has been recorded and as a result he has been seriously prejudiced. The order of conviction and sentence as against the appellant on the basis of such so called admission of guilt cannot therefore be sustained in law the case should be sent back remand to the Trial Court.

Md. Shaheb Ali Miah Vs The State 3BLT (HCD)-110

Section-243

Against the order of acquittal passed by the learned Magistrate, there is provision for appeal- the learned Sessions Judge has acted illegally and without jurisdiction in] entertaining the revisional application under section 439A Cr. P. C. against the order of acquittal passed by the learned Magistrate-the order of the learned Sessions Judge, liable to be set aside.

Abdul Aziz Khan & Ors Vs. The State 2 BLT (HCD)-94

Section-247

Section 247 confers a discretion upon the trial Magistrate to adjourn the hearing of a case, when the complainant fails to appear; on the date, if the Court thinks that there are good reasons for non-appearance! Obviously, the trial Magistrate did not think it proper to adjourn the hearing of the case when the complainant failed to appear - the trial Magistrate rightly passed the order of acquittal under section 247 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

M. Mofizuddin Vs. Abdul Kalam & Ors 4 BLT (AD)-149

Section-247

A complaint case ought not to be dismiss for non-appearance of the complainant on adjourned date unless he/she attends in t Court of the Magistrate is specially require on that date or unless the Trial Court f convinced that the complainant is not keen on prosecuting his case. In the instant case it appears that the complainant tool adjournments by filing petition on the ground of illness supported by medical certificate and the impugned order bears reasoning as to why the learned Magistrate of the  dismissed  the  petition  for non appearance of the complainant. It is not clear as to whether the learned Magistrate dismissed the petition of complaint holding that the claim of the complainant or that she is taking adjournment in order to harass the accused. In view of the such facts and circumstances we are unable to support the impugned order and as such the same is liable to be set aside.

A. Jabber Howlader Vs. Ali Akbar Howlader & Ors. 8 BLT (HCD)-62

Section-247

Abuse of the process of Law—intentional default in appearing before the Court

There is no legal bar to entertain fresh petition of complain on the self same allegation even after disposal of the prior e under section 247 of the Code Criminal Procedure. BLT we hold the view that there should be limit to such type of privilege. If it is found that the petitioner is making default in appearing before the Court intentionally there after he was in the habit of filing fresh petitions of complain one after another with ulterior motive, the Magistrate should his discretion in refusing to entertain fresh petition of complain for the 3rd time as in the present case, if he finds no cogent ground for the prior of defaults. Because such type of practice if allowed without applying judicial mind would not only cause sufferings and unusual harassment to the opposite party BLT also it amounts to sheer abuse of the process of law and stands in the way of even handed dispensation of justice.

Habibur Rahman Vs Feroj Ahmed & Ors. 12 BLT (HCD)-277

Section - 247

Section 247 of the Code of Criminal lure is not applicable in a case where complainant asked for adjournment. Application filed for adjournment does not absent in prosecution BLT absent for some other cause on that date.

Abdul Hadi Vs. The State & Anrs. BLT (HCD)-211

Section-265-1

The Code of Criminal Procedure, in its section 265-1 has made a provision for the accused person to enter upon his defence. BLT it all depends upon the accused to avail or not. The accused person himself could cross-examine the witnesses and put forward his defence Case. No one, at the appellate stage, is entitled to a benefit out of his own laches.

Jahangir Alam Vs. The State 15 BLT (HCD)191

Section-265-1(3)

The application under section 265-1(3) of the code of Criminal Procedure was filed on 3.3.2003 soon after the completion of deposition of the P.Ws. and the accused were examined under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and in support of their plea of innocence and false implication in the case the Courts below should have allowed the said application as the same was not vexatious or to cause unnecessary delay or for defeating the ends of justice in view of the defence plea, instead there is likelihood of the petitioner's being prejudiced for not allowing the said application.

Foyez Ahmed Vs. The State 12 BLT (AD)128

Section-265- B

The Plea of guilty of appellant in the midst of the trial of the Case.

This plea of guilty is not legal plea of guilty at all. A plea of guilty in a criminal Court can only be made in response to a charge made by the Court. In this case the charge was framed on 05.02.2002 and P.W-1 was examined on 10.07.2001 and his plea was accepted on 26.08.2001.

Sheikh Mujibur Rahman @ Razibulla & Ors. Vs. The State 11 BLT (HCD)-262

Section-265 C

The learned Counsel for the petitioner contends that in the present case Mr. Uno Mong S.I. of police who was not the Investigation Officer recorded the statements of some witnesses without any requisition from the Investigation Officer but the High Court Division failed to appreciate this legal position - Held : Furthermore it cannot now be ascertained that the person who recorded the statement of the witnesses was not authorized or requested to do that. It can only be determined at the time of trial while examining the Investigation Officer and if it is found that the person who recorded the statement of certain witnesses was not authorized to such recording or has not been requisitioned for the purpose the trial court may take appropriate decision if they are examined during trial but at this stage it cannot be found that there is no material to frame charge against the petitioners.

Nurul Islam Manzoor & Ors. vs. The State 9 BLT (AD)-214

Section - 265C

The provisions of section 265-C and 265-B are mandatory. It cast duty upon the court to scrutinize the record at the document submitted there before discharging or framing a charge in a case as the case may be. Just because name of the particular person is mentioned in FIR or charge sheet is not sufficient to frame charge against him or frame charge mechanically so that innocent persons may not be harassed on false and vexatious allegations.

Debobrota Baiddya Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD)-24

Charged under Section 201 of the Penal Code- The learned Additional Sessions] Judge considered the statements of the witnesses recorded under section 161 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and framed charge against the accused respondent! The State VS. Khondker Md. Moniruzzaman 5 BLT (AD)-9

Section-265-E

A plea of guilty is not a confession such as is dealt with the Evidence Act in view of the fact that there are not pleadings in a criminal Court and an accused person cannot be judged in a criminal case, by how he pleads" or fails to plead in the proceeding. The plea of guilty must distinctly admit each and every fact necessary to constitute the offence. An accused person pleads guilty to the facts which purports to disclose and offence under that section.

Sheikh Mujibur Rahman @ Razibulla & Ors. Vs. The State 11 BLT (HCD)-262

Section-295A read with Section-561A

An article was published in the Daily Jana Kantha under the capital " ?? ??? ?????? ???????? ???????” : writer used nick name as” Klanto Pathik” which according to the complainant disstorted the meaning of Sura "Tin of the Holy Quran—Held: The intention of the publication was to make the real Muslim aware about the false interpretation given by so-called half educated and self claimed preachers of Islam in the society. In fact, the petitioners who are also a group of Muslim intelligentsia intended to alert the Muslims general against the half educated or non-educated Islamic thinkers who dominate a portion of Islamic people in our society—so allegation does not come within the ambit of the offence of Section-295A of Penal Code against the petitioners-proceedings the complaint case are quashed.

Section-337 and 338

Section 337 and 338 of The Code are to read and applied together. The pardon is, thus, conditional, condition being disclosure of the whole circumstances of the commission of crime.

Section-338 read with Evidence Act, 1872

Law, thus is not that the evidence of an accomplice outright rejection and liable to flung to the wind if there is no corroboration. What is required is to adopt great circumspection and care when dealing the the  testimony of  an accomplice. Though there is no legal necessity to seek corroboration of an accomplice evidence it desirable that the court seeks reassuring circumstances to satisfy the judicial conscience that the evidence is true.

State Vs. Ershad Ali Sikder & Anr. 11 BLT (HCD)-102

Section-339C

The order of conviction and sentence could not be set aside on a mere technicality and further that the respondents not having availed of the benefit under section 339C at the trial state, they could not be allowed the said benefit after the conclusion of the trial and that also at the revision stage as contended by the informant petitioners Advocate:

Held: If the trial was held in contravention of the prescribed procedure as laid down, it cannot be said to be a trial in accordance with law and the consequence as provided in the procedure itself must follow.

Narayan Chandra Goswami Vs. B. N. Chakrabarty   3 BLT (AD)-139

Section-339 (C)

Working days mean the working days of the trial Judge and not of the Court and as such if the concerned Judge is on leave that period of leave must also be excluded in computing the statutory of period of the working days for holding the trial of the case as contended by the learned Advocate for the State.

Held: The principle regarding calculating of working days settled in the decision reported in 40 DLR (AD) 97 is very clear on the point urged before us and the same is binding on this Court.

Abdul Khayer & Ors Vs. The State 4 BLT (HCD)-89

Section-339C

Bail- in Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Case

It appears that the Court adjourned the trial of the case on every fixed date with direction to issue summons or W.W. against the witness. The trial of a case under the Nari-O-Shishu Nirjatan Daman Ain, 1995, should not be delayed in the manner as is being in this case although the informant appeared and filed several application for cancellation of bail of the accused Shamsunnahar. He being the informant is the first witness in this case but the first witness, although being present in Court, has not been examined till today. We depricate this kind of delaytory tactics by keeping the accused in hajat for an indefinite period without knowing when the trial can be concluded. In such facts and circumstances, we find that the accused appellant is entitled to get benefit of section 339C Cr. P. C. for the purpose of bail.

Sohel Vs. The State 7BLT(HCD)-283

Section-339C(4)

The question that arises in the instant case is that during the pendency of the Criminal revision before the High Court Division a new provision introduced by Act No XLII of 1992 came into force and this being a procedural law whether it will apply to a pending case.

Held: In view of the repeal of sub-section (4) of section 389C Cr.P.C. followed by re-enactment of the said sub-section the new procedural law will be applicable in the pending cases although instituted when the old provision was in force and the pending cases are to be governed by the new procedure under the amended law- In our considered opinion the provision of sub­section (4) of section 339C of the Code of Criminal Procedure as amended by Act No. XLII of 1992 will be applicable to the pending cases.

Abdul Wadud Vs. The State 3 BLT (AD)-236

Section-339C(4)

The case record in question was received by the learned Assistant Sessions Judge on 16.09.90 but no charged was framed till 17.3.92 and the accused have been kept in custody beyond the period of as provided to Section 2 (B) of ordinance 50 of 1982. Subsequently by Act 42 of 1992, repeal of the said law on 1st November, 1992- Held: We must admit that the Act 41 of 1992 there is no reference about its) retrospective effect. So it appears that the accused petitioners have retained vested right in getting the case disposed of within 240 days on receipt of the case by the triaK court and since the learned trial court failed to dispose of the case within the stipulated time i.e. within 240 days the learned Assistant Sessions Judge ought to have entertained the petition and thereby stopped the proceeding and release the accused petitioner therefrom.

Moklesur Rahman & Ors Vs. The State 6 BLT (HCD)-186

Section-339C(4)

We are of the view that in the said provision; there is no absolute direction to allow bail to the accused, even in case of failure to? complete the trial within the statutory period, as the mandate, if any, for allowing! such bail has been subjected by the words, "Unless for reasons to be released in writing the Court otherwise directs," The jurisdiction to direct otherwise, refusing bail even in case of such happening i.e. failure to complete the trial within the statutory period had therefore been kept.

Nurul Islam Monzoor Vs. The State & Ors 9 BLT (HCD)-57

Md. Nur Israil Talukder Vs. the State 7 BLT (AD)-17

Section-339D(1) (b)

(a) Aggrieved persons- Petitioner being the full brother of the deceased victim and a charge-sheeted prosecution witness is an aggrieved person.

(b) Cogent grounds for revival of the case-with the creation of a new Session Division, the learned Senior Judges posted there, could not remain present regularly and consequently he could not attend court regularly in spite of his efforts, the application by the accused for stopping the proceeding was heard ex parte only on presence of the learned Advocate for the accused petitioners, the wrong calculation of the working days could not be brought to the police of their lordships while disposing of the Criminal Revision Case, these are cogent reasonable grounds for revival of a cases.

Abdus Sobhan Vs Ali Akbar & Ors 3 BLT (HCD)-10

Section-340 (3) with a provision in Sub-Section-3

Intention of the legislature for inserting such provision enabling the accused to adduce evidence on oath, in our opinion, is to prove the plea of alibi specifically set up by the accused for absolving him from criminal liability particularly when the wife has been killed in the house of the husband or vice versa.

Yunus & Ors. Vs. The State 8 BLT (HCD)245

Section- 342

The purpose of examination of the accused persons under Section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is to bring to their notice all incriminating pieces of evidence to be used against them for affording the accused on opportunity to offer their explanation thereto for consideration of the Court. This is, no doubt, a valuable statutory right of the accused and it is by no means an idle ceremony or a mere routine-work for the trial Court. This provision of law is intended for the benefit of the accused and as such the trial Court is under an obligation to properly comply with the requirement of law so as to avoid any possible prejudice to the accused.

Due to careless exercise made by the trial Courts, sometimes the provisions of Section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure are rendered nugatory necessitating remand of a case to the trial Court for removing the legal deficiency, causing unnecessary prejudice to the accused as well as to the prosecution.

Alhaz Nurul Alam Chowdhury & Anr. Vs. The State 7 BLT (HCD)-SO

Section-342

The provision of Section 342 Cr. P. C. has been codified by the legislature providing opportunity to the accused concerned to make out his case about his innocence of the offence. Charged, but he was denied his right to present his case for no fault of his own as he was in Government Custody. So the accused petitioner has been seriously prejudiced.

Shahidul Vs. the State 7BLT (HCD)-142

Section-342

Incriminating circumstances appearing in the evidence of PWs particularly of PW1 complainant having not been pointed out to the accused of the present case, during 342 Cr. P.C. statement, he is likely to be gravely prejudiced in his defence.

Nibash chandra Sarker Vs. Dipali Rani & Anr. 8 BLT (HCD)-29

Section-342

Substantial justice — The purpose of examination under section 342 is to explain the circumstance against the accused stating the evidence in support of the charges but in the instant case the only material before the Court against the accused respondent was the confessional statement of Co-accused which is no legal evidence against the convict respondent in the absence of any other corroborative evidence. Admittedly there is no eyewitness to the occurrence and there was not corroboration of the confessional statement of the co-accused implicating the accused respondent the accused respondent implicating in the case. — In that view of the matter in order to secure substantial justice in the case we are inclined to set aside the impugned judgment setting the aside conviction and sentence and sending back the case to the trial from the stage of his examination under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure while rejecting the reference.

The State Vs. Md. Tuku Biswas 11 BLT (AD)-92

Section -342

Section 342 of The Code is the mandatory provision for procedural law and a departure from fundamental principle of section 342 of The Code causes prejudice to the accused. This section confers a valuable] right of the accused and at the same time gives an opportunity to the court to: administer justice in accordance with fundamental principle of criminal justice. It is eminent that it is the duty of the court to] question accused properly and fairly; bringing home to his mind in clear and simple language the exact case he has to, meet and each material point that is sought] to be made against him and of affording him a chance to explain them if he can and so desires. Sub-section 3 of Section 342 of the Code contains necessary support to the legal position that answers given by the accused] during such examination are intended to be considered by the court. The words "it may! be taken into consideration in such inquiry! or trial " in sub-section 3 of Section 342 of the Code would amount to a legislative guideline for the court to give due weight to such answers though it does not mean that such answers could be made the sole basis of any finding.

The State Vs. Sabir Mia & ors. 11 BLT (HCD)-294

Section-342

Extra Judicial Confession The condemned prisoner in reply to his examination under section 342 Cr. P.C. was that as per advise of the informant A. Latif, he took his elder sister Aleya for working an his house, that they jointly worked at his] house at monthly wage of Tk.500/- but he did not pay their wages regularly, that Aleya used to sleep in the house of A. atif while he was sleeping in the shallow machine room, that Latif had developed illicit relationship with Aleya, for which, she became pregnant and that he shirked the responsibility upon Sirajul after killing her.

Held: The evidence of extra judicial confession is always taken as very weak type of evidence. The Courts require some material corroboration to such a confessional statement but from the evidence on record we find that the witnesses disclose the uttering of the accused in different manners. The surrounding circumstances and the evidence P.Ws.l, 2, 3 and 12, indicate that the informant on suppressing the real incident has set up this story. None of them corroborates each other as to the manner, the mode and the place of making extra judicial confession by the accused. In that view of the matter, we are of the opinion that the prosecution has miserably failed to prove at accused Sirajul Islam has made any extra judicial confession in the manner as stated by it and that the defence version is more probable than that of the prosecution. The learned Sessions Judge has totally ignored the inconsistent statements of P.Ws.l, 2, 3 and 12 as regards their stories that the accused Sirajul has made extra judicial confession in their presence and convicted the condemned prisoner on the basis of his inconsistent extra judicial confession.

State Vs. Md. Sirajul Islam 12 BLT (HCD) 328

Section - 342

Convict-appellant at the time of his examination under section 342 of The Code bestowed a written statement and insisted his innocence and false implication in the case. Convict-appellant in the written statement presented full picture of the case programmed by him and explained circumstances which led PW 1 and his family member to implicate him in the false case. Convict-appellant, also, under a list placed papers and documents in support of the contents comprised in the written statement. Learned Trial Judge did not at all care to take into account the written statement and the documents and papers enclosed in the written statement in support of convict-appellant's innocence. Learned Trial Judge did not write a single word not to speak a sentence on the written statement and documents and papers enclosed with the written statement. Non-consideration of written statement and documents and papers in support of written statement by learned Trial Judge and his absolute silence on those caused a prejudice of a grave nature to convict-appellant and by non-consideration the merit of the decision of the case had been materially affected.

Kazi Mahbubuddin Ahmed Vs. The State 13 BLT (HCD)-524

Section-342

The learned Trial Court based its finding to the alleged extra-judicial confession made by accused-appellant Asiruddin followed by recovery of certain bones, but with utter surprised we may record that the learned Trial Court did not notice that the same fact was stated to the accused-appellant Asiruddin who at the time of his examination u/s 342 of the Cr. P. C. allegedly made extra-judicial confession (basis of conviction) and as such it is held that he could not have opportunity to give his reply about the same and in view of such facts and circumstances the basis of conviction (as claimed by the Trial Court) appears to have vitiated the entire findings.

Asiruddin @ Asir Dakat & Ors. Vs. The State 13 BLT (HCD)-389

Section - 342

The provision engrafted in section 342 is intended to comply with the most salutary principles of natural justice enshrined in the maxim "audi altarem partem".

Sharafat Mondal & Ors. Vs. The State & Ors 14 BLT (HCD)-290

Section -342

Non application of mind —On running an eye to the examination under section 342 of The Code it demonstrates that, though, no case had been projected and no evidence had been led to the effect that the convict-appellants with edged weapon mounted attack upon informant's son Masudul Islam Masud (deceased), Delwar Hossain (PW 7) and caused injury upon Delwar Hossain (PW7) and killed Abul kalam (convict) but in examination under section 342 of the code each of the convict-appellants had been put to the question that convict-appellants with sharp weapon attacked informant's son Masudul Islam Masud (deceased), Delwar Hossain (PW.7) and wounded Delwar Hossain (PW.7) and killed Abul Kalam and committed offence of section 302/34 of penal code. Abul Kalam was not murdered rather Abul Kalam had been depicted as the assailant who had given a farewell to the life of Masudul Islam and Masudul Islam was done to death. This type of examination is a demonstration of highest degree of non-application of mind on the part of learned Trial Judge which is highly deprecated and disparaged.

Aminul Islam & Ors Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD)-420

Section-342

read with Section 537

When the accused is able to understand the nature of accusations brought against him, and the evidence have been taken in his presence and He is prudent enough to furnish a statement in disprove of his guilt, it cannot be said that strict non-compliance of the provisions of section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure has, in any way prejudiced his defence, though this Court has always desired so.

Shahabuddin Vs The State 13 BLT (HCD) 411

Section -342

No prosecution case had been installed and no evidence had been led that convict appellants Jahangir Alam and Mukut caus serious bleeding injury on the right side the chest of deceased Ajoy Kumar and, also that they caused swelling injury on different parts of the body but they were put questions in the terms that they generated serious bleeding injury on the right side of the chest of deceased Ajoy Kumar and, also caused swelling injuries on different parts of his body. Again the essence of the testimonies of prosecution witnesses and other incriminating circumstances had n been at all put to the convict-appellants, close exploration of the examination of t" convict-appellants and other accused persons under section 342 of The Co indicates that a synopsis of the accusation brought home against the convict-appellants and other accused persons had been put. Learned Trial Judge, though, had stated that the accused persons heard examination witnesses but essence of the testimonies all the twelve prosecution witnesses connecting convict-appellants in the crime and other incriminating circumstances had not been at all placed -Held; Provision contained in section 342 of The Code appeared to have been not at all followed and convict-appellants had been highly prejudiced by impermissive examination under section 342 of The Code.

Touhid & Ors Vs. the State 15 BLT (HCD) 364

Sections- 342 And 537

It is settled law that exculpatory statement uncorroborated by any other evidence, since the attention was not drawn to the confessional statement of the confessing accused when he was examined under section 342 he is obviously prejudiced and his trial therefore has been vitiated. Such defect is not curable under Section- 537 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

Abu Jamal & Ors. Vs. The State 7BLT (HCD)-252

Section- 342 Read with Section- 537

The confessional statement on scrutiny has been found to be true and voluntary and the

same gets corroboration from some other evidence also, appellant had been not prejudiced for non mentioning of his confession in his examination under section 342 Cr.P.C. is curable under section 537 Cr.P.C. in the facts and circumstances of the case and the same cannot and has not vitiated the trial as alleged.

Abul Khayer & Ors Vs. The State 4 BLT (HCD)-89

Section- 344

The question of stay is one of judicial discretion of the court having regard to the facts and circumstances of a given case-if the finding of the civil suit is likely to prejudice the accused then the question of stay should be given favourable consideration- The principle governing the stay of proceeding of civil suit vis-à-vis criminal cases is that the criminal matters should be given precedence.

A B Siddikur Rahman Vs. A M Harunur Rashid & Ors 3 BLT (AD)-64

Section- 344

The hearing of case No. 33 was concluded and 25.9.1993 was fixed for judgment but the delivery of judgment has remained pending, on the ground of pendency of the counter case No. 34 which it appears, is still in the midst of examination of witnesses-long thereafter the informant in Case No. 33 moved the Sessions Judge in revision on 8.3.1995 against the aforesaid order dated 25.9.1993.  The  learned  Sessions Judge rejected the revision petition holding that the same was hopelessly time barred. Then the informant  came  upto the  High Court Division with an application under section 561A Cr.P.C. which was summarily rejected by a Division Bench.

Held: The Sessions Judge of the High Court division pught to have given a direction to the Magistrate for concluding the trial in case No. 34 quickly as the other case No. 33 was awaiting Judgment for nearly two years- it does not give credit to the Sessions Judge to have ignored the aforesaid facts and to have disposed of the revision petition wrongly by a mere fiat that it was hopelessly time-barred.

Mantasir Billah Vs. Bepari Abdur Rab & Ors 3 BLT (AD)-185

Section-344(1)

An accused person may be remanded if it is likely that in the interest of investigation into an offence further evidence is to be obtained and Magistrate is not precluded from handing over the accused to the police for the purpose of investigation in a case or some other cases in which the accused is involved. Order of remand dated 26.2.2005 for a period of 10 days and, thereafter, on 9.3.2005 for a period of another 10 days with a gap of three days are not liable to be declared to have been made and passed illegally, arbitrarily and malafidely. Petitioner is not at all entitled to be favoured with an order that orders of remand are illegal, arbitrary and malafide.

A. A. Sakib Vs. The State 14 BLT (HCD) 402.
